## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on amplitude)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 + c2 * x**3 (nonlinear damping and restoring)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric + cubic restoring + damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**3 (coupled nonlinear terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, xآ³, xâپµ) preserve symmetry of oscillation; even powers (xآ²) indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation/injection; sign determines damping vs anti-damping
- Products of xآ² and v (e.g., xآ²*v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type oscillators
- Explicit time dependence typically appears through trigonometric functions cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) representing periodic external forcing
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or self-regulated
- Cubic position terms (xآ³) with opposite sign to linear term (x) indicate a double-well or hardening/softening spring potential
- Odd-symmetry in velocity damping (vآ³, v|v|) preserves time-reversal antisymmetry of dissipation
- Parametric excitation manifests as multiplicative coupling between time-periodic functions and position: cos(c*t)*x
